<p><b>Heidelberg</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈhaɪdl̩bɛʁk]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/Heidelberg.ogg" class="internal" title="Heidelberg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>) is a <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">college town</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a> situated on the river <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> in south-west <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. At the 2015 census, its population was 156,257, with roughly a quarter of its population being students.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Located about 78&#160;km (48&#160;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Heidelberg is the fifth-largest city in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">German state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>. Heidelberg is part of the densely populated <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Neckar" title="Rhine-Neckar">Rhine-Neckar Metropolitan Region</a>.</p>
<p>Founded in 1386, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> is Germany's oldest and one of Europe's most reputable universities.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific hub</a> in Germany, the city of Heidelberg is home to several internationally renowned <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg#Research" title="Heidelberg">research facilities</a> adjacent to its university, including four <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Institutes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>A former residence of the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a>, Heidelberg is a popular <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourist destination</a> due to its <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romantic</a> cityscape, including <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg#Philosophers.27_Walk" title="Heidelberg">Philosophers' Walk</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque style</a> Old Town.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg/220px-Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg/330px-Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg/440px-Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg-luftbild-aerial-photograph.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg with suburbs</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heidelberg is in the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Rift_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine Rift Valley">Rhine Rift Valley</a>, on the left bank of the lower part of the Neckar in a steep valley in the <a href="/wiki/Odenwald" title="Odenwald">Odenwald</a>. It is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königsstuhl</a> (568&#160;m) and the <a href="/wiki/Gaisberg_(Heidelberg)" title="Gaisberg (Heidelberg)">Gaisberg</a> (375&#160;m) mountains. The Neckar here flows in an east-west direction. On the right bank of the river, the <a href="/wiki/Heiligenberg_(Heidelberg)" title="Heiligenberg (Heidelberg)">Heiligenberg</a> mountain rises to a height of 445 meters. The Neckar flows into the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> approximately 22 kilometres north-west in <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>. Villages incorporated during the 20th century stretch from the Neckar Valley along the Bergstraße, a road running along the <a href="/wiki/Odenwald" title="Odenwald">Odenwald</a> hills.</p>
<p>Heidelberg is on <a href="/wiki/European_walking_route_E1" class="mw-redirect" title="European walking route E1">European walking route E1</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>-<a href="/wiki/Umbria" title="Umbria">Umbria</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg/220px-Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg/330px-Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg/440px-Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2034" data-file-height="1528" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Stadtteile_2012.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The districts of Heidelberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_from_the_K%C3%B6nigstuhl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg seen from <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königstuhl</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since Heidelberg is among the warmest regions of Germany, plants atypical of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">central-European</a> climate flourish there, including <a href="/wiki/Almond" title="Almond">almond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">fig trees</a>; there is also an <a href="/wiki/Olive_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive tree">olive tree</a> in <i>Gaisbergstraße</i>. Alongside the <i>Philosophenweg</i> (Philosophers' Walk) on the opposite side of the Old Town, <a href="/wiki/Winegrowing" class="mw-redirect" title="Winegrowing">winegrowing</a> was restarted in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a wild population of African <a href="/wiki/Rose-ringed_parakeet" title="Rose-ringed parakeet">rose-ringed parakeets</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and a wild population of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> <a href="/wiki/Swan_goose" title="Swan goose">swan geese</a>, which can be seen mainly on the islands in the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> near the district of Bergheim.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_structures">Administrative structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Administrative structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg/220px-Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg/330px-Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg/440px-Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="778" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Altstadt_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Altstadt</i> from the Castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heidelberg is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority#Germany" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> within the Regierungsbezirk Karlsruhe. The <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Neckar-Kreis" title="Rhein-Neckar-Kreis">Rhein-Neckar-Kreis</a> rural district surrounds it and has its seat in the town, although the town is not a part of the district. Heidelberg is a part of the Rhine-Neckar Metropolitan Region, often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Neckar-Triangle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhein-Neckar-Triangle">Rhein-Neckar Triangle</a>.</p>
<p>This region consists of the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">State</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hessen" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessen">Hessen</a>, the southern part of the State of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a> (<i>Vorderpfalz</i>), the administrative districts of <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> and Heidelberg, and the southern municipalities of the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Neckar-Kreis" title="Rhein-Neckar-Kreis">Rhein-Neckar-Kreis</a>. The Rhein-Neckar Triangle became a European <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> in 2005.</p>
<p>Heidelberg consists of 15 districts distributed in six sectors of the town. In the central area are Altstadt (the Old Town), <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-Bergheim" title="Heidelberg-Bergheim">Bergheim</a> and Weststadt; in the north, Neuenheim and Handschuhsheim; in the east, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-Ziegelhausen" title="Heidelberg-Ziegelhausen">Ziegelhausen</a> and Schlierbach; in the south, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-S%C3%BCdstadt" title="Heidelberg-Südstadt">Südstadt</a>, Rohrbach, Emmertsgrund, and Boxberg; in the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-Kirchheim" title="Heidelberg-Kirchheim">Kirchheim</a>; in the west, Pfaffengrund, Wieblingen, and a new district, named <i>Bahnstadt</i>, is built on land in Weststadt and Wieblingen. The new district will have approximately 5,000–6,000 residents and employment for 7,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighbouring_communes">Neighbouring communes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Neighbouring communes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following towns and <a href="/wiki/Commune" title="Commune">communes</a> border the city of Heidelberg, beginning in the west and in a clockwise direction: <a href="/wiki/Edingen-Neckarhausen" title="Edingen-Neckarhausen">Edingen-Neckarhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dossenheim" title="Dossenheim">Dossenheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schriesheim" title="Schriesheim">Schriesheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmsfeld" title="Wilhelmsfeld">Wilhelmsfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nau_(Odenwald)" title="Schönau (Odenwald)">Schönau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neckargem%C3%BCnd" title="Neckargemünd">Neckargemünd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bammental" title="Bammental">Bammental</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaiberg" title="Gaiberg">Gaiberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leimen_(Baden)" title="Leimen (Baden)">Leimen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandhausen" title="Sandhausen">Sandhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oftersheim" title="Oftersheim">Oftersheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plankstadt" title="Plankstadt">Plankstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eppelheim" title="Eppelheim">Eppelheim</a> (all part of the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Neckar-Kreis" title="Rhein-Neckar-Kreis">Rhein-Neckar-Kreis</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heidelberg has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Cfb</i>), defined by the protected valley between the Pfälzerwald and the Odenwald. Year-round, the mild temperatures are determined by maritime air masses coming from the west. In contrast to the nearby <a href="/wiki/Upper_Rhine_Plain" title="Upper Rhine Plain">Upper Rhine Plain</a>, Heidelberg's position in the valley leads to more frequent easterly winds than average. The hillsides of the Odenwald favour clouding and precipitation. The warmest month is July, the coldest is January. Temperatures often rise beyond 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F) in <a href="/wiki/Midsummer" title="Midsummer">midsummer</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Wetterdienst" title="Deutscher Wetterdienst">German Meteorological Service</a>, Heidelberg was the warmest place in Germany in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg" class="image" title="This panorama from the Theodor-Heuss-Brücke shows the Neckar running through Heidelberg. On the left is Neuenheim, with its Neckarwiesen (Neckar meadows); on the right is the Altstadt."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg/900px-07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg" width="900" height="182" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg/1350px-07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg/1800px-07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8093" data-file-height="1639" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:07.07.22.Heidelberg_Neckar.jpg" title="File:07.07.22.Heidelberg Neckar.jpg"></a></div>
This panorama from the Theodor-Heuss-Brücke shows the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> running through Heidelberg. On the left is Neuenheim, with its <i>Neckarwiesen</i> (Neckar meadows); on the right is the <i>Altstadt</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_nachts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Heidelberg_nachts.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_nachts.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Heidelberg_nachts.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_nachts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Heidelberg_nachts.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_nachts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_nachts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg on the Neckar at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe_207.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Karlsplatz and Neckar with Old Bridge</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 600,000 and 200,000 years ago<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, "<a href="/wiki/Homo_heidelbergensis" title="Homo heidelbergensis">Heidelberg Man</a>" died at nearby <a href="/wiki/Mauer_(Baden)" title="Mauer (Baden)">Mauer</a>. His jaw bone was discovered in 1907. Scientific dating determined his remains as the earliest evidence of human life in Europe. In the 5th century BC, a <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> fortress of refuge and place of worship were built on the <i>Heiligenberg</i>, or "Mountain of Saints". Both places can still be identified. In 40 AD, a fort was built and occupied by the 24th Roman cohort and the 2nd <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaican" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrenaican">Cyrenaican</a> cohort (CCG XXIIII and CCH II CYR). The Romans built and maintained <i><a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">castra</a></i> (permanent camps) and a signal tower on the bank of the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>. They built a wooden bridge based on stone pillars across it. The camp protected the first civilian settlements that developed. The Romans remained until 260 AD, when the camp was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Germanic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic people">Germanic tribes</a>. The local administrative center in roman times was the nearby city of <a href="/wiki/Ladenburg" title="Ladenburg">Lopodunum</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Modern Heidelberg can trace its beginnings to the fifth century. The village <i>Bergheim</i> ("Mountain Home") is first mentioned for that period in documents dated to 769 AD. <i>Bergheim</i> now lies in the middle of modern Heidelberg. The people gradually converted to Christianity. In 863 AD, the <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastery</a> of <a href="/wiki/St._Michael" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Michael">St. Michael</a> was founded on the <a href="/wiki/Heiligenberg_(Heidelberg)" title="Heiligenberg (Heidelberg)">Heiligenberg</a> inside the double rampart of the Celtic fortress. Around 1130, the Neuburg Monastery was founded in the Neckar valley. At the same time, the bishopric of <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> extended its influence into the valley, founding <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nau_Abbey" title="Schönau Abbey">Schönau Abbey</a> in 1142. Modern Heidelberg can trace its roots to this 12th-century monastery. The first reference to Heidelberg can be found in a document in <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nau_Abbey" title="Schönau Abbey">Schönau Abbey</a> dated to 1196. This is considered to be the town's founding date. In 1155, Heidelberg castle and its neighboring settlement were taken over by the house of <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufen" title="Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a>. <a href="/wiki/Conrad_of_Hohenstaufen" class="mw-redirect" title="Conrad of Hohenstaufen">Conrad of Hohenstaufen</a> became <a href="/wiki/Count_Palatine_of_the_Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="Count Palatine of the Rhine">Count Palatine of the Rhine</a> (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Pfalzgraf bei Rhein</span>). In 1195, the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a> passed to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">House of Welf</a> through marriage.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Blechen_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Carl_Blechen_003.jpg/220px-Carl_Blechen_003.jpg" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Carl_Blechen_003.jpg/330px-Carl_Blechen_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Carl_Blechen_003.jpg/440px-Carl_Blechen_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2536" data-file-height="2197" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Blechen_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>, here shown in a painting by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Blechen" title="Carl Blechen">Carl Blechen</a>, was destroyed by the French during the war of succession of the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_-_panoramio_(39).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_-_panoramio_%2839%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_-_panoramio_(39).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of castle from the Corn Market</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1214, <a href="/wiki/Louis_I,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Louis I, Duke of Bavaria">Ludwig I, Duke of Bavaria</a> acquired the Palatinate, as a consequence of which the castle came under his control. By 1303, another castle had been constructed for defense. In 1356, the Counts Palatine were granted far-reaching rights in the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_1356" title="Golden Bull of 1356">Golden Bull</a>, in addition to becoming <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Electors</a>. In 1386, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Rupert_I,_Elector_Palatine" title="Rupert I, Elector Palatine">Rupert I, Elector Palatine</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heidelberg University played a leading part in the era of humanism and the Reformation, and the conflict between Lutheranism and Calvinism, in the 15th and 16th centuries. Heidelberg's library, founded in 1421, is the oldest existing public library in Germany. In April 1518, a few months after proclaiming his 95 Theses, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> was received in Heidelberg, to defend them. In 1537, the castle located higher up the mountain was destroyed by a gunpowder explosion. The duke's palace was built at the site of the lower castle.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg/220px-Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg" width="220" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg/330px-Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg/440px-Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="1212" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belagerung_Heidelbergs_C-L_205.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The siege of Heidelberg 1622</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Elector_Frederick_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Elector Frederick III">Elector Frederick III</a>, sovereign of the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Palatinate" title="Electoral Palatinate">Electoral Palatinate</a> from 1559 to 1576, commissioned the composition of a new Catechism for his territory. While the catechism's introduction credits the "entire theological faculty here" (at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Heidelberg" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Heidelberg">University of Heidelberg</a>) and "all the superintendents and prominent servants of the church" for the composition of the catechism, Zacharius Ursinus is commonly regarded as the catechism's principal author. <a href="/wiki/Caspar_Olevianus" class="mw-redirect" title="Caspar Olevianus">Caspar Olevianus</a> (1536–1587) was formerly asserted as a co-author of the document, though this theory has been largely discarded by modern scholarship. <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sylvan" title="Johann Sylvan">Johann Sylvan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Neuser" title="Adam Neuser">Adam Neuser</a>, Johannes Willing, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Erastus" title="Thomas Erastus">Thomas Erastus</a>, Michael Diller, Johannes Brunner, Tilemann Mumius, Petrus Macheropoeus, Johannes Eisenmenger, <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Tremellius" title="Immanuel Tremellius">Immanuel Tremellius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Boquin" title="Pierre Boquin">Pierre Boquin</a> are all likely to have contributed to the Catechism in some way. Frederick himself wrote the preface to the Catechism and closely oversaw its composition and publication. Frederick, who was officially Lutheran but had strong Reformed leanings, wanted to even out the religious situation of his highly Lutheran territory within the primarily Catholic <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> had just concluded with its conclusions and decrees against the Protestant faiths, and the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a> had only granted toleration for <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> within the empire where the ruler was Lutheran. One of the aims of the catechism was to counteract the teachings of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> as well as Anabaptists and "strict" <a href="/wiki/Gnesio-Lutherans" title="Gnesio-Lutherans">Gnesio-Lutherans</a> like <a href="/wiki/Tilemann_Heshusius" title="Tilemann Heshusius">Tilemann Heshusius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Flacius" title="Matthias Flacius">Matthias Flacius</a>, who were resisting Frederick's Reformed influences, particularly on the matter of Eucharist (<a href="/wiki/The_Lord%27s_Supper" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lord's Supper">the Lord's Supper</a>). The Catechism-based each of its statements on biblical proof-texts, and Frederick himself would defend it as biblical, not reformed, at the 1566 Diet of Augsburg when he was called to answer to charges of violating the Peace of Augsburg. This was the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Catechism" title="Heidelberg Catechism">Heidelberg Catechism</a>, officially called the ″Catechism, or Christian Instruction, according to the Usages of the Churches and Schools of the Electoral Palatinate.″</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe,_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg/220px-2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg/330px-2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg/440px-2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe%2C_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1563" data-file-height="1172" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2002-04-02_Hauptstra%C3%9Fe,_Heidelberg_IMG_0404.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main street Heidelberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In November 1619, the royal crown of Bohemia was offered to the Elector, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_V,_Elector_Palatine" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick V, Elector Palatine">Frederick V</a>. (He was married to <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth of Bohemia">Elizabeth</a>, eldest daughter of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a> of Scotland and England, respectively.) Frederick became known as the "Winter King", as he reigned for only one winter before the Imperial <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> regained the crown by force. His overthrow in 1621 marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>. In 1622, after a <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Heidelberg_(1622)" title="Siege of Heidelberg (1622)">siege of two months</a>, the armies of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(German)" title="Catholic League (German)">Catholic League</a>, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Tserclaes,_Count_of_Tilly" title="Johann Tserclaes, Count of Tilly">Johann Tserclaes, Count of Tilly</a>, captured the town. Tilly gave the famous <i><a href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Palatina" title="Bibliotheca Palatina">Bibliotheca Palatina</a></i> from the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Spirit,_Heidelberg" title="Church of the Holy Spirit, Heidelberg">Church of the Holy Spirit</a> to the Pope as a present. The Catholic Bavarian branch of the House of Wittelsbach gained control over the Palatinate and the title of Prince-Elector. In 1648, at the end of the war, Frederick V's son <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_Louis,_Elector_Palatine" title="Charles I Louis, Elector Palatine">Charles I Louis, Elector Palatine</a>, was able to recover his titles and lands.</p>
<p>In late 1634 Imperialist forces attempted to take back the city, as the Swedish army had conquered it. They quickly took the city, but were unable to take the castle. As they prepared to blow up its fortifications with gunpowder the French army arrived, 30,000 men strong, led by <a href="/wiki/Urbain_de_Maill%C3%A9-Br%C3%A9z%C3%A9" title="Urbain de Maillé-Brézé">Urbain de Maillé-Brézé</a>, who had fought in many battles and participated in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_La_Rochelle" title="Siege of La Rochelle">Siege of La Rochelle</a> (1627–1628), and <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Nompar_de_Caumont,_duc_de_La_Force" title="Jacques-Nompar de Caumont, duc de La Force">Jacques-Nompar de Caumont, duc de La Force</a>. They ended the siege and drove off the Catholic forces.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotelritter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Hotelritter.jpg/220px-Hotelritter.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Hotelritter.jpg/330px-Hotelritter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Hotelritter.jpg/440px-Hotelritter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1432" data-file-height="2154" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotelritter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hotel zum Ritter St. Georg.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To strengthen his dynasty, Charles I Louis arranged the marriage of his daughter <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Charlotte,_Princess_Palatine" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth Charlotte, Princess Palatine">Liselotte</a> to <a href="/wiki/Philip_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip I, Duke of Orléans">Philip I, Duke of Orléans</a>, brother of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV</a>, king of France. In 1685, after the death of Charles Louis' son, Elector <a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Elector_Palatine" title="Charles II, Elector Palatine">Charles II</a>, Louis XIV laid claim to his sister-in-law's inheritance. The Germans rejected the claim, in part because of religious differences between local Protestants and the French Catholics, as the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> had divided the peoples of Europe. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Grand_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Grand Alliance">War of the Grand Alliance</a> ensued. In 1689, French troops took the town and castle, bringing nearly total destruction to the area in 1693. As a result of the destruction due to repeated French invasions related to the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Palatinate_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Palatinate Succession">War of the Palatinate Succession</a> coupled with severe winters, thousands of Protestant German Palatines emigrated from the lower Palatinate in the early 18th century. They fled to other European cities and especially to London (where the refugees were called "the poor Palatines"). In sympathy for the Protestants, in 1709–1710, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne's</a> government arranged transport for nearly 6,000 Palatines to New York. Others were transported to <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>. They worked their passage and later settled in the English colonies there.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg/220px-Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg/330px-Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg/440px-Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1496" data-file-height="1119" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Bruecke_Heidelberg_von_Konrad_Linck_1788.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old Bridge, Konrad Linck, 1788</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1720, after assigning a major church for exclusively Catholic use, religious conflicts with the mostly Protestant inhabitants of Heidelberg caused the Roman Catholic Prince-Elector <a href="/wiki/Karl_III_Philip,_Elector_Palatine" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl III Philip, Elector Palatine">Charles III Philip</a> to transfer his residence to nearby <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>. The court remained there until the Elector <a href="/wiki/Charles_Theodore,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Charles Theodore, Elector of Bavaria">Charles Theodore</a> became <a href="/wiki/Rulers_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Rulers of Bavaria">Elector of Bavaria</a> in 1777 and established his court in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. In 1742, Elector Charles Theodore began rebuilding the Palace. In 1764, a lightning bolt destroyed other palace buildings during reconstruction, causing the work to be discontinued.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1803_to_1933">1803 to 1933</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1803 to 1933">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heidelberg fell to the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Baden" title="Grand Duchy of Baden">Grand Duchy of Baden</a> in 1803. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Frederick,_Grand_Duke_of_Baden" title="Charles Frederick, Grand Duke of Baden">Charles Frederick, Grand Duke of Baden</a>, re-founded the university, named "Ruperto-Carola" after its two founders. Notable scholars soon earned it a reputation as a "royal residence of the intellect". In the 18th century, the town was rebuilt in the Baroque style on the old medieval layout.</p>
<p>In 1810, the <a href="/wiki/French_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="French revolution">French revolution</a> refugee Count Charles Graimberg began to preserve the palace <a href="/wiki/Ruins" title="Ruins">ruins</a> and establish a historical collection. In 1815, the Emperor of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, the Emperor of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and the King of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> formed the "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Alliance" title="Holy Alliance">Holy Alliance</a>" in Heidelberg. In 1848, the German National Assembly was held there. In 1849, during the Palatinate-Baden rebellion of the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_German_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the German states">1848 Revolutions</a>, Heidelberg was the headquarters of a revolutionary army. It was defeated by a Prussian army near Waghaeusel. The city was occupied by Prussian troops until 1850. Between 1920 and 1933, Heidelberg University became a center of notable physicians Czerny, Erb, and Krehl; and humanists Rohde, Weber, and Gandolf.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nazism_and_the_World_War_II-period">Nazism and the World War II-period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Nazism and the World War II-period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_Heidelberg_Germany_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Old_Bridge_(Heidelberg)" title="Old Bridge (Heidelberg)">Old Bridge Gate</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the Nazi period (1933–1945), Heidelberg was a stronghold of the <a href="/wiki/NSDAP" class="mw-redirect" title="NSDAP">NSDAP</a>, (the National Socialist German Workers' Party) the strongest party in the elections before 1933 (the NSDAP obtained 30% at the communal elections of 1930<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>). The NSDAP received 45.9% of the votes in the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_March_1933" title="German federal election, March 1933">German federal election of March 1933</a> (the national average was 43.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Non-<a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan</a> university staff were discriminated against. By 1939, one-third of the university's teaching staff had been forced out for racial and political reasons. The non-Aryan professors were ejected in 1933, within one month of Hitler's rise to power. The lists of those to be deported were prepared beforehand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (October 2010)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1934 and 1935, the <i>Reichsarbeitsdienst</i> (State Labor Service) and Heidelberg University students built the huge <i>Thingstätte</i> amphitheatre on the <i>Heiligenberg</i> north of the town, for <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a> events. A few months later, the inauguration of the huge Ehrenfriedhof memorial cemetery completed the second and last NSDAP project in Heidelberg. This cemetery is on the southern side of the old part of town, a little south of the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königstuhl</a> hilltop, and faces west towards France. During World War II and after, <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> soldiers were buried there.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Synagogue_Memorial_Stone,_1_Lauerstrasse,_Heidelberg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG/220px-Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG/330px-Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG/440px-Synagogue_Memorial_Stone%2C_1_Lauerstrasse%2C_Heidelberg.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Synagogue_Memorial_Stone,_1_Lauerstrasse,_Heidelberg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial stone marking the site of the synagogue in the Lauerstrasse</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> on November 9, 1938, Nazis burned down synagogues at two locations in the city. The next day, they started the systematic deportation of Jews, sending 150 to <a href="/wiki/Dachau_concentration_camp" title="Dachau concentration camp">Dachau concentration camp</a>. On October 22, 1940, during the "Wagner Buerckel event", the Nazis deported 6000 local Jews, including 281 from Heidelberg, to <a href="/wiki/Camp_Gurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Camp Gurs">Camp Gurs</a> concentration camp in France. Within a few months, as many as 1000 of them (201 from Heidelberg) died of hunger and disease.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Among the deportees from Heidelberg, the poet <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Mombert" title="Alfred Mombert">Alfred Mombert</a> (1872–1942) left the camp in April 1941 thanks to the Swiss poet Hans Reinhart.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> From 1942, the deportees who had survived internment in Gurs were deported to Eastern Europe, where most of them were murdered.</p>
<p>On March 29, 1945, German troops left the city after destroying three arches of the old bridge, Heidelberg's treasured river crossing. They also destroyed the more modern bridge downstream. The U.S. Army (63rd Infantry, 7th Army) entered the town on March 30, 1945. The civilian population surrendered without resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>A popular belief is that Heidelberg escaped bombing in World War II because the U.S. Army wanted to use the city as a garrison after the war. As Heidelberg was neither an industrial center nor a transport hub, it did not present a target of opportunity. Other notable university towns, such as <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCbingen" title="Tübingen">Tübingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ttingen" title="Göttingen">Göttingen</a>, were spared bombing as well. Allied air raids focused extensively on the nearby industrial cities of <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludwigshafen" title="Ludwigshafen">Ludwigshafen</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg/220px-The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg/330px-The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg/440px-The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1422" data-file-height="890" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_ferrying_troops_and_vehicles_over_the_Neckar_River_at_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">US Army</a> <a href="/wiki/289th_Engineer_Combat_Battalion_(United_States)" title="289th Engineer Combat Battalion (United States)">289th Engineer Combat Battalion</a> ferrying troops and vehicles over the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> at Heidelberg.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The U.S. Army may have chosen Heidelberg as a garrison base because of its excellent infrastructure, including the Heidelberg-Mannheim <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> (motorway), which connected to the Mannheim-Darmstadt-Frankfurt Autobahn, and the U.S. Army installations in <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. The intact rail infrastructure was more important in the late 1940s and early 1950s when most heavy loads were still carried by train, not by lorry. Heidelberg had the untouched Wehrmacht barracks, the "Grossdeutschland Kaserne" which the US Army occupied soon after, renaming it the <a href="/wiki/Campbell_Barracks" title="Campbell Barracks">Campbell Barracks</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_after_1945">History after 1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: History after 1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1945, the university was reopened relatively quickly on the initiative of a small group of professors, among whom were the anti-Nazi economist <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Weber" title="Alfred Weber">Alfred Weber</a> and the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Karl_Jaspers" title="Karl Jaspers">Karl Jaspers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The surgeon Karl Heinrich Bauer was nominated rector.</p>
<p>On December 9, 1945, US Army General <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a> had a car accident in the adjacent city of Mannheim and died in the Heidelberg US Army hospital on December 21, 1945. The funeral ceremony was held at the Heidelberg-Weststadt <i>Christuskirche</i> (Christ Church), and he was buried in the 3rd Army cemetery in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the post-war <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">military occupation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Army" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Army">U.S. Army</a> used the <i><a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Thingst%C3%A4tte" title="Heidelberg Thingstätte">Thingsstätte</a></i> for cultural and religious events. Civilian use started in the early to mid-1980s for occasional concerts and other cultural events. Today, the celebrations on <i>Hexennacht</i> ("Witches' Night"), also called <a href="/wiki/Walpurgis_Night" title="Walpurgis Night">Walpurgis Night</a>), the night of April 30, are a regular "underground" fixture at the <i>Thingstätte</i>. Thousands of mostly young people congregate there to drum, to breathe fire, and to juggle. The event has gained fame throughout the region, as well as a certain notoriety due to the amount of litter left behind.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_population.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Heidelberg_population.svg/220px-Heidelberg_population.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Heidelberg_population.svg/330px-Heidelberg_population.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Heidelberg_population.svg/440px-Heidelberg_population.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_population.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population growth</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The population of the city of Heidelberg exceeded 100,000 for the first time in 1946. It is a city with an international population, including one of the largest American communities outside North America, but this is not analysed in the Heidelberg population statistics. At the end of December 2011, the city had 149,633 inhabitants with an official primary residence in Heidelberg (not including the soldiers and employees of the U.S. Army and their dependents, a total of about 20,000 people), a historic high.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following table shows the number of inhabitants within the boundaries of the city at the time. To 1833 they are mostly estimates, then census results or official updates of the statistical offices of the time or the city administration. The data refer from 1843 to the "local population", from 1925 to the resident population and since 1987 the "population at the site of their main dwelling." Prior to 1843 the population was determined by non-uniform collection procedures.</p>

<p>With a <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> of 1.1 children per woman in the <i>Stadtkreis</i> (county), Heidelberg had the lowest fertility rate in Baden-Württemberg in 2008.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right;">
<tr style="background:#cde;">

<p>Since 2006, the <i>Oberbürgermeister</i> (lord mayor) of Heidelberg has been the independent Eckart Würzner. From 1990 to 2006, the mayor was Beate Weber (SPD).</p>
<p>The council consists of 40 volunteer members with the mayor as chairman. The council is directly elected for a term of five years. The task of the council is to decide with the mayor presiding all the affairs of the city. The council controls the city administration and oversees the enforcement of its decisions.</p>
<p>Heidelberg has always been a stronghold of the Greens. For the municipal elections in 2009, they split into the Green Alternative List and Alliance 90/The Greens and each ran their own lists. Together they gained 10 seats to become the strongest force for the first time.</p>
<p>After the election, the deputies of the Alliance 90/The Greens formed a coalition with generation.HD. In September 2011 two members of the GAL Group joined the Alliance 90/The Greens, so now with generation.HD, they form the largest group in the council.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_old_town">The old town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The old town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg/220px-2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg/330px-2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg/440px-2002-04-02_Heidelberger_Rathaus_IMG_0388.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1582" data-file-height="935" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG/220px-Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG/330px-Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG/440px-Deutschland_Heidelberg_Schloss.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_winter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Heidelberg_winter.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_winter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Heidelberg_winter.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_winter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Heidelberg_winter.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_winter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_winter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from the castle during winter, 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "old town" (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Altstadt</span>), on the south bank of the Neckar, is long and narrow. It is dominated by the ruins of <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>, 80 metres above the Neckar on the steep wooded slopes of the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königstuhl</a> (<i>King's chair or throne</i>) hill.</p>
<ul>
<li>The Main Street (<i>Hauptstrasse</i>), a mile-long pedestrian street, running the length of the old town.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Old_Bridge_(Heidelberg)" title="Old Bridge (Heidelberg)">old stone bridge</a> was erected 1786–1788. A medieval bridge gate is on the side of the old town, and was originally part of the town wall. Baroque tower helmets were added as part of the erection of the stone bridge in 1788.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Spirit,_Heidelberg" title="Church of the Holy Spirit, Heidelberg">Church of the Holy Spirit</a> (<i>Heiliggeistkirche</i>), a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">late Gothic</a> church in the marketplace of the old town.</li>
<li>The Karls‘ gate (<i>Karlstor</i>) is a triumphal arch in honour of the Prince Elector Karl Theodor, located at Heidelberg's east side. It was built 1775–1781 and designed by Nicolas de Pigage.</li>
<li>The house <i>Zum Ritter Sankt Georg</i> (Knight St. George) is one of the few buildings to survive the War of Succession. Standing across from the Church of the Holy Spirit, it was built in the style of the late <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>. It is named after the sculpture at the top.</li>
<li>The <i>Marstall</i> (Stables), a 16th-century building on the Neckar that has served several purposes through its history. It is now a cafeteria for the university.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heidelberg_Castle">Heidelberg Castle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Heidelberg Castle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg/220px-Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg/330px-Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg/440px-Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1977" data-file-height="2066" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plan_des_Heidelberger_Schlosses_von_Peter_Friedrich_von_Walpergen_um_1780.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historic map of <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_(10).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_%2810%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_17.11.2012_-_panoramio_(10).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg Castle at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG/220px-Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG/330px-Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG/440px-Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Schloss_Luftbild_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg Fortress</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The castle is a mix of styles from <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a>. Prince Elector Ruprecht III (1398–1410) erected the first building in the inner courtyard as a royal residence. The building was divided into a ground floor made of stone and framework upper levels. Another royal building is located opposite the Ruprecht Building: the Fountain Hall. Prince Elector Philipp (1476–1508) is said to have arranged the transfer of the hall's columns from a decayed palace of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ingelheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingelheim">Ingelheim</a> to Heidelberg.</p>
<p>In the 16th and 17th centuries, the Prince Electors added two palace buildings and turned the fortress into a castle. The two dominant buildings at the eastern and northern side of the courtyard were erected during the rule of Ottheinrich (1556–1559) and Friedrich IV (1583–1610). Under Friedrich V (1613–1619), the main building of the west side was erected, the so-called "English Building".</p>
<p>The castle and its garden were destroyed several times during the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> and the Palatine War of Succession. As Prince Elector Karl Theodor tried to restore the castle, lightning struck in 1764, and ended all attempts at rebuilding. Later on, the castle was misused as a quarry; stones from the castle were taken to build new houses in Heidelberg. This was stopped in 1800 by Count Charles de Graimberg, who then began the process of preserving the castle.</p>
<p>Although the interior is in Gothic style, the King's Hall was not built until 1934. Today, the hall is used for festivities, e.g. dinner banquets, balls and theatre performances. During the Heidelberg Castle Festival in the summer, the courtyard is the site of open air musicals, operas, theatre performances, and classical concerts performed by the Heidelberg Philharmonics.</p>
<p>The castle is surrounded by a park, where the famous poet <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann von Goethe</a> once walked. The <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_Bergbahn" title="Heidelberger Bergbahn">Heidelberger Bergbahn</a> <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular</a> railway runs from Kornmakt to the summit of the Königstuhl via the castle.</p>
<h3><span id="Philosophers'_Walk"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophers.27_Walk">Philosophers' Walk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Philosophers' Walk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the northern side of the Neckar is located the Heiligenberg (<i>Saints' Mountain</i>), along the side of which runs the Philosophers' Walk (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Philosophenweg</span>), with scenic views of the old town and castle. Traditionally, Heidelberg's philosophers and university professors would walk and talk along the pathway. Farther up the mountain lie the ruined 11th-century <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_St._Michael_(Heidelberg)" title="Monastery of St. Michael (Heidelberg)">Monastery of St. Michael</a>, the smaller Monastery of St. Stephen, a Nazi-era amphitheater, the so-called Pagan's hole and the remains of an earthen <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hill_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill fort">hill fort</a> from the 4th century BC.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_on_the_old_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/View_on_the_old_Heidelberg.jpg/700px-View_on_the_old_Heidelberg.jpg" width="700" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a9/View_on_the_old_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="944" data-file-height="150" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_on_the_old_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from the so-called "Philosophers' Walk" (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Philosophenweg</span>) towards the Old Town, with <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Heiliggeist_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Heidelberg Heiliggeist church">Heiliggeist Church</a> and the Old Bridge</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heidelberg_churches">Heidelberg churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Heidelberg churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are many historical churches in Heidelberg and its surroundings. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Spirit,_Heidelberg" title="Church of the Holy Spirit, Heidelberg">Church of the Holy Spirit</a> has been shared over the centuries since the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> by both Catholics and Protestants. It is one of the few buildings to survive the many wars during the past centuries. It was rebuilt after the French set fire to it in 1709 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Grand_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Grand Alliance">War of the Palatinian Succession</a>. The church has remains of the tombs and epitaphs of the past Palatinate electors. This Church stands in the <i>Marktplatz</i> next to the seat of local government. In 1720, Karl III Philip, Elector Palatine came into conflict with the town's Protestants as a result of giving the Church of the Holy Spirit exclusively to the Catholics for their use. It had previously been split by a partition and used by both congregations. Due to pressure by the mostly Protestant powers of Prussia, Holland, and Sweden, Prince Karl III Philip gave way and repartitioned the church for joint use. In 1936 the separating wall was removed. The church is now exclusively used by Protestants. Furthermore, there is the Catholic Church of the Jesuits. Its construction began in 1712. It was completed with the addition of a bell tower from 1866–1872. The church is also home to the Museum für sakrale Kunst und Liturgie (Museum of <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecclesiastical">Ecclesiastical</a> Arts). The oldest church in Heidelberg is the St. Peter's Church (now <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>). It was built some time during the 12th century.</p>
