<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities_and_academia">Universities and academia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Universities and academia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Heidelberg_people" class="mw-redirect" title="List of University of Heidelberg people">List of University of Heidelberg people</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidlbergaula.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Heidlbergaula.JPG/220px-Heidlbergaula.JPG" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Heidlbergaula.JPG/330px-Heidlbergaula.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Heidlbergaula.JPG/440px-Heidlbergaula.JPG 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="388" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidlbergaula.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old university hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg/220px-Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg/330px-Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b2/Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="372" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Normal_Uni-Bibliothek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The university library</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heidelberg is known for its institutions of higher education. The most famous of those is <b><a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a></b>. Founded in 1386, it is one of Europe's oldest institutions. In fact, Heidelberg is the oldest <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">university town</a> of today's Germany. Among the prominent thinkers associated with the institution are <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Jaspers" title="Karl Jaspers">Karl Jaspers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans-Georg_Gadamer" title="Hans-Georg Gadamer">Hans-Georg Gadamer</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Habermas" title="Jürgen Habermas">Jürgen Habermas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl-Otto_Apel" title="Karl-Otto Apel">Karl-Otto Apel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Arendt" title="Hannah Arendt">Hannah Arendt</a>. The campus is situated in two urban areas and several buildings. In numerous historical buildings in the old town there are the Faculties of the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">Humanities</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Social_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Science">Social Science</a> and the Faculty of <a href="/wiki/Jurisprudence" title="Jurisprudence">Law</a>. The school of applied sciences is located in the <i>Science Tower</i> in Wieblingen. The Faculties of Medicine and <a href="/wiki/Natural_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Science">Natural Science</a> are settled on the Neuenheimer Feld Campus.</p>
<p>Since 1904 there has been a College of Educational Science, the <i>Pädagogische Hochschule Heidelberg</i>; since 1979 there has been a college of Jewish Studies, the <i>Hochschule für Jüdische Studien Heidelberg</i>. It comprises nine branches specializing on both religion and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish culture</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Schiller_International_University" title="Schiller International University">Schiller International University</a>, a private American university is also represented with a campus in Heidelberg offering several undergraduate and graduate programs in the fields of International Business and International Relations and Diplomacy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg/220px-EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg/330px-EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg/440px-EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="632" data-file-height="253" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EMBL_campus_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buildings of <a href="/wiki/European_Molecular_Biology_Laboratory" title="European Molecular Biology Laboratory">European Molecular Biology Laboratory</a> in Heidelberg, including the new Advanced Training Centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LSW-Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/LSW-Heidelberg.jpg/220px-LSW-Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/LSW-Heidelberg.jpg/330px-LSW-Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/LSW-Heidelberg.jpg/440px-LSW-Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="614" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LSW-Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-K%C3%B6nigstuhl_State_Observatory" title="Heidelberg-Königstuhl State Observatory">Heidelberg-Königstuhl State Observatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the research centers and institutes of the university, there are numerous research institutions situated in the city of Heidelberg. Among them are the <a href="/wiki/European_Molecular_Biology_Laboratory" title="European Molecular Biology Laboratory">European Molecular Biology Laboratory</a> (EMBL), <a href="/wiki/European_Molecular_Biology_Organization" title="European Molecular Biology Organization">European Molecular Biology Organization</a> (EMBO), the <a href="/wiki/German_Cancer_Research_Center" title="German Cancer Research Center">German Cancer Research Center</a> (DKFZ), <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Medical_Research" title="Max Planck Institute for Medical Research">Max Planck Institute for Medical Research</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Astronomy" title="Max Planck Institute for Astronomy">Max Planck Institute for Astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Nuclear_Physics" title="Max Planck Institute for Nuclear Physics">Max Planck Institute for Nuclear Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Comparative_Public_Law_and_International_Law" title="Max Planck Institute for Comparative Public Law and International Law">Max Planck Institute for Comparative Public Law and International Law</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg/220px-Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg/330px-Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg/440px-Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fachhochschule_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
SRH Hochschule Heidelberg is one of the oldest and largest private universities in Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heidelberg is home to 23 elementary schools. There are several institutions of secondary education, both public and private, representing all levels of the <a href="/wiki/German_school_system" class="mw-redirect" title="German school system">German school system</a>. There are 14 <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">Gymnasiums</a>, with six of them private. With 52% of secondary students attending a Gymnasium, Heidelberg sits above the German average, perhaps because a large number of academics live in Heidelberg and its environs.</p>
<p>They include the Kurfürst-Friedrich-Gymnasium (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurf%C3%BCrst-Friedrich-Gymnasium_Heidelberg" class="extiw" title="de:Kurfürst-Friedrich-Gymnasium Heidelberg">German Wikipedia</a>), Bunsen-Gymnasium (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bunsen-Gymnasium_Heidelberg" class="extiw" title="de:Bunsen-Gymnasium Heidelberg">German Wikipedia</a>), the Helmholtz-Gymnasium (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helmholtz-Gymnasium_Heidelberg" class="extiw" title="de:Helmholtz-Gymnasium Heidelberg">German Wikipedia</a>), the Hölderlin-Gymnasium and the Elisabeth-von-Thadden-Schule. Then there are seven <a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschule</a>, ten <a href="/wiki/Hauptschule" title="Hauptschule">Hauptschule</a> and nine <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational schools</a> (the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Berufsschule" class="mw-redirect" title="Berufsschule">Berufsschule</a></i>). In addition, there are several <a href="/wiki/Folk_high_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk high schools">folk high schools</a> with different specialisations.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_International_School" title="Heidelberg International School">Heidelberg International School</a> serves the local expatriate community.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, 81.8% of people worked for service industries, including tourism. As a relic of the period of Romanticism, Heidelberg has been labeled a "Romantic town". This is used to attract more than 3.5 million visitors every year. Many events are organized to attract visitors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Only 18% of employment is provided by industry. Printing and publishing are important enterprises; nearby <a href="/wiki/Walldorf" title="Walldorf">Walldorf</a> is a center of the IT industry and <a href="/wiki/SAP_SE" title="SAP SE">SAP</a> World Headquarters. Noted pen manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Lamy" title="Lamy">Lamy</a> has its headquarters and factory in Heidelberg-Wieblingen. <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen" title="Heidelberger Druckmaschinen">Heidelberger Druckmaschinen</a> has its headquarters here; its factory is located in Walldorf. Soft-drink company Wild-Werke, manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/Capri-Sonne" class="mw-redirect" title="Capri-Sonne">Capri-Sonne</a> (<a href="/wiki/Capri-Sun" class="mw-redirect" title="Capri-Sun">Capri-Sun</a> in the U.S.) is located nearby in Eppelheim. Heidelberg is also home to the headquarters of HeidelbergCement, the world's second largest cement producer. The Company has its roots in the suburb of Leimen where one of its cement plants is still located. With its long Hauptstrasse, Heidelberg is a shopping destination for people from the surrounding smaller towns.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg/220px-Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg/330px-Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg/440px-Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1592" data-file-height="2020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberger_Druckmaschinen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Print Media Academy</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_5" title="Bundesautobahn 5">A 5 autobahn</a> runs through the western outskirts of Heidelberg, connecting the region to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> in the north and <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">Karlsruhe</a> to the south. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_656" title="Bundesautobahn 656">A 656</a> commences just west of the city, connecting Heidelberg with <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>. Both highways meet at Heidelberg autobahn intersection in the city of Heidelberg, and the A 656 connects to the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_6" title="Bundesautobahn 6">A 6</a> at the Mannheim autobahn intersection, which connects to the east towards <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>.</p>
<p>Furthermore, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_3" title="Bundesstraße 3">B 3</a> (Frankfurt–Karlsruhe) runs north–south through the town, and the B 37 (Mannheim–<a href="/wiki/Eberbach_(Baden)" title="Eberbach (Baden)">Eberbach</a>) runs east–west. Both meet in the city center at the Bismarckplatz. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_535&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundesstraße 535 (page does not exist)">B 535</a> begin in the south of Heidelberg and runs to Schwetzingen.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_roads">Tourist roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tourist roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Heidelberg is located on four tourist roads: <a href="/wiki/Bergstra%C3%9Fe_Route" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergstraße Route">Bergstraße</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bertha_Benz_Memorial_Route" title="Bertha Benz Memorial Route">Bertha Benz Memorial Route</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Road" title="Castle Road">Castle Road</a>, and Straße der Demokratie (Road of Democracy).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Heidelberg Central Station">Heidelberg Central Station</a> (Hauptbahnhof) is on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Valley_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine Valley Railway">Rhine Valley Railway</a> and is served by <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">Intercity-Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/EuroCity_in_Germany" title="EuroCity in Germany">Euro City</a> trains. This station is served by the <a href="/wiki/RheinNeckar_S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="RheinNeckar S-Bahn">RheinNeckar S-Bahn</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png/220px-Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png/330px-Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png/440px-Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="3508" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stra%C3%9Fenbahnlinien_Heidelberg.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg tramway network</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg/170px-Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg/255px-Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg/340px-Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1640" data-file-height="2095" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bergbahn_Koenigstuhl_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_Bergbahn" title="Heidelberger Bergbahn">funicular</a> at <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königstuhl</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main transport hub of Heidelberg is the Bismarckplatz. Several main thoroughfares of the city intersect here and one of the longest pedestrian streets in Europe, the Hauptstraße (main street) runs from here through the entire old town of Heidelberg. Heidelberg Central Station was nearby for many years, which was a combined terminal and through station. In 1955, it was moved about 1.5&#160;km further to the west, which removed the necessity for trains continuing to the south or from the south to the north to reverse. The new central station became the second major transport hub of Heidelberg.</p>
<p>Heidelberg has had a public transport service since 1883, when horse-drawn trams were established. Due to the rapidly rising patronage it was decided on 20 December 1901 to convert the <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Heidelberg" title="Trams in Heidelberg">Heidelberg tramway network</a> to electrical operation. On 16 March 1902, the first electric tram ran on Rohrbacher Straße, sharing use of the suburban tracks built by the <i>Deutsche Eisenbahn-Gesellschaft</i> in 1901 between Heidelberg and <a href="/wiki/Wiesloch" title="Wiesloch">Wiesloch</a>. Until the 1950s, the tram network was expanded a bit at a time. The rapidly growing popularity of car transport presented the operator of the trams with increasingly difficult problems and the tram network was gradually dismantled. It was not until 10 December 2006 that the network was extended again with the opening of a new tram line from <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg-Kirchheim" title="Heidelberg-Kirchheim">Kirchheim</a>. Tram and bus services are now operated by <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Neckar-Verkehr" title="Rhein-Neckar-Verkehr">Rhein-Neckar-Verkehr</a> (RNV). Since 1989, all fares are set under a uniform scheme by the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Rhein-Neckar" title="Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Neckar">Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Neckar</a> (Rhine-Neckar Transport Association, VRN). <a href="/wiki/Carsharing" title="Carsharing">Carsharing</a> increasingly provides a complement to public transport. More than 50 car-sharing stations are available to users in 12 of the 14 districts of Heidelberg offering a total of more than 100 cars.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Line 24 tram in Rohrbach</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 14 December 2003, Heidelberg has been connected to the network of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Neckar_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Neckar S-Bahn">Rhine-Neckar S-Bahn</a>, which opens up the entire Rhine-Neckar region, with lines connecting with the <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_(region)" title="Palatinate (region)">Palatinate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_Bergbahn" title="Heidelberger Bergbahn">Heidelberger Bergbahn</a> (Heidelberg Mountain Railway) has run since 2005 with new cars on the lower part from Kornmarkt to Molkenkur and historic cars built in 1907 on the upper section of the <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular</a> from Molkenkur to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstuhl_(Odenwald)" title="Königstuhl (Odenwald)">Königstuhl</a>. It is one of the most popular means to reach <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>. The first plans for the funicular were drawn up in 1873. Due to a lack of funds was the first section of the funicular was not opened until 1890. In 2004, the upper section of the funicular was listed as part of the heritage of the state of Baden-Württemberg.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_military_installations">United States military installations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: United States military installations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Garrison_Heidelberg" title="United States Army Garrison Heidelberg">United States Army Garrison Heidelberg</a></div>
<p>During World War II, Heidelberg was one of the few major cities in Germany not significantly damaged by Allied bombing. Situated in the <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany#American_Zone_of_Occupation" title="Allied-occupied Germany">American Zone</a> of Germany, Heidelberg became the headquarters of the American forces in Europe. Several military installations remain, including <a href="/wiki/Campbell_Barracks" title="Campbell Barracks">Campbell Barracks</a>, the former Wehrmacht Grossdeutschland-Kaserne, where headquarters for several units are located. These include US Army, Europe (<a href="/wiki/USAREUR" class="mw-redirect" title="USAREUR">USAREUR</a>) and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s Component Command-Land Headquarters. (Until 2004, this was designated Joint Headquarters Centre, and before that, LANDCENT).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg/220px-Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg/330px-Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg/440px-Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Behoerdenzentrum_Heidelberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Behördenzentrum Heidelberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG/220px-Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG/330px-Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG/440px-Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Bahnstadt_Langer_Anger_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New city district of Heidelberg, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahnstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bahnstadt (page does not exist)">Bahnstadt</a>, is one of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Passive_house" title="Passive house">passive house</a> settlements in the world</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Campbell Barracks and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain_Village" title="Mark Twain Village">Mark Twain Village</a> are both in Südstadt; Patton Barracks is in nearby Kirchheim. Nachrichten Kaserne in Rohrbach is home to the former Heidelberg Army Hospital, now designated the Heidelberg Health Center. <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry_Village" title="Patrick Henry Village">Patrick Henry Village</a>, the largest U.S. military housing area in the Heidelberg area, is west of Kirchheim. These installations, including Tompkins Barracks and Kilbourne Kaserne in nearby Schwetzingen, plus the Germersheim Depot, used to make up the U.S. Army Garrison Heidelberg. Tompkins Barracks is home to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.imcom-europe.army.mil">U.S. Army Installation Management Command Europe Region.</a> The Heidelberg U.S. Army Air Field (Heidelberg AAF) was converted to a<s>n</s> heliport (mostly Blackhawk Helicopters) after the NATO Kosovo campaign.</p>
<p>The children of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> employees based in Heidelberg tend to attend on-base schools operated by the DODDS-E (Department of Defense Dependents Schools&#160;– Europe). There are three schools of this kind: <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_High_School" title="Heidelberg High School">Heidelberg High School</a> in Mark Twain Village (Mark Twain Elementary School closed at the completion of the 2010–2011 school year), and <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Middle_School" title="Heidelberg Middle School">Heidelberg Middle School</a> and Patrick Henry Elementary in Patrick Henry Village.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 19, 2009 the U.S. Army announced that it will be building new headquarters for USAREUR in <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>. The move from Heidelberg will take place in 2012 and 2013, and will be completed by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> By 2015 all United States forces will have moved out of Heidelberg. The barracks and the housing areas will be handed over to the German state for conversion to civilian use.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg/220px-Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg/330px-Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg/440px-Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theater_und_Orchester_Heidelberg_-_Au%C3%9Fenansicht.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Theater_%26_Orchester_Heidelberg" title="Theater &amp; Orchester Heidelberg">Theater &amp; Orchester Heidelberg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Heidelberg_night.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_night.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Heidelberg_night.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Heidelberg_night.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heidelberg with the Old Bridge illuminated</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the year there are different regular festivals and events hosted and organized in Heidelberg. In February, the <i>Ball der Vampire</i> (Ball of the Vampires)<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> is arranged and Fasching, the equivalent of Mardis Gras or Carnival in some German regions, with a giant vampire-themed costume party at the local castle or city hall is celebrated. In March or April the <i>Heidelberger Frühling</i> (Heidelberg Spring), the Classic Music Festival and the international Easter egg market are conducted. During the last weekend of April there is an annually organized half marathon. In the summertime there are the <i>Frühlingsmesse</i> on the Messeplatz (May) and Illumination of the castle and bridge with lights and fireworks take place. In September, on the last Saturday the <i>Old Town Autumn Festival</i> is held.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It includes a Medieval Market, an arts and crafts market, a flea market, and music from Samba to Rock. During October or November there are the <i>Heidelberger Theater Days</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Enjoy_Jazz" title="Enjoy Jazz">Enjoy Jazz</a> festival. Every year in November the <a href="/wiki/International_Filmfestival_Mannheim-Heidelberg" title="International Filmfestival Mannheim-Heidelberg">International Filmfestival Mannheim-Heidelberg</a> take place in the city, too. The festival presents arthouse films of international newcomer directors and is held jointly by both of the cities.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> During Christmas there is a Christmas market throughout the oldest part of the city. A famous gift is the chocolate called Heidelberger <i>Studentenkuss</i> (student kiss).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinemas">Cinemas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cinemas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Karlstorkino offers an arthouse program, rare classics and feature films. Here, most films are shown in original version. The Harmonie Lux has had a rather mainstream Hollywood program before its closing in 2014, whilst the small independent cinemas Gloria &amp; Gloriette as well as Kamera also show arthouse films, mostly in German versions. Plans for a new Luxor-Kino in the new district Bahnstadt, featuring both blockbusters and arthouse films, have been in the works since 2013 and the construction began in July, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_exhibitions">Museums and exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Museums and exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Among the most prominent museums of Heidelberg are for instance the Carl Bosch Museum which shows life and work of chemist and Nobel Prize-winner <a href="/wiki/Carl_Bosch" title="Carl Bosch">Carl Bosch</a>. Then there is the <a href="/wiki/Documentation_and_Culture_Centre_of_German_Sinti_and_Roma" class="mw-redirect" title="Documentation and Culture Centre of German Sinti and Roma">Documentation and Culture Centre of German Sinti and Roma</a> (Dokumentations- und Kulturzentrum Deutscher Sini und Roma) describing the Nazi genocide of the <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> peoples. The German Packing Museum (Deutsches Verpackungsmuseum) gives an overview on the history of packing and wrapping goods whereas the German Pharmacy Museum (Deutsches Apothekenmuseum) which is located in the castle illustrates the story of Pharmacy in Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Kurpf%C3%A4lzisches_Museum" title="Kurpfälzisches Museum">Kurpfälzisches Museum</a> (Palatinate Museum) offers a great art collection and some Roman archeological artifacts from the region. In the honour of <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Ebert" title="Friedrich Ebert">Friedrich Ebert</a> one established the <a href="/wiki/President_Friedrich_Ebert_Memorial" title="President Friedrich Ebert Memorial">President Friedrich Ebert Memorial</a> which remembers the life of Germany's first democratic head of state. Besides, there are guided tours in most of the historical monuments of Heidelberg, as well as organized tourist tours through the city available in several languages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heidelberg_Romanticism">Heidelberg Romanticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Heidelberg Romanticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg/220px-Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg/330px-Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg/440px-Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1805" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Philipp_Fohr_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Romantic view of <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a> ruins</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heidelberg was the centre of the epoch of <i>Romantik</i> (<a href="/wiki/German_Romanticism" title="German Romanticism">Romanticism</a>) in Germany. The phase after <a href="/wiki/Jena_Romanticism" title="Jena Romanticism">Jena Romanticism</a> is often called <b>Heidelberg Romanticism</b> (see also <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Romanticism" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Romanticism">Berlin Romanticism</a>). There was a famous circle of poets (the <b>Heidelberg Romantics</b>), such as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_von_Eichendorff" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph von Eichendorff">Joseph von Eichendorff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Joseph_von_G%C3%B6rres" class="mw-redirect" title="Johann Joseph von Görres">Johann Joseph von Görres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Achim_von_Arnim" title="Ludwig Achim von Arnim">Ludwig Achim von Arnim</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clemens_Brentano" title="Clemens Brentano">Clemens Brentano</a>. A relic of Romanticism is the Philosophers' Walk (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Philosophenweg</span>), a scenic walking path on the nearby Heiligenberg, overlooking Heidelberg.</p>
<p>The <i>Romantik</i> epoch of German philosophy and literature, was described as a movement against classical and realistic theories of literature, a contrast to the rationality of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>. It elevated medievalism and elements of art and narrative perceived to be from the medieval period. It also emphasized folk art, nature and an epistemology based on nature, which included human activity conditioned by nature in the form of language, custom and usage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Heidelberg">Old Heidelberg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Old Heidelberg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Alt_Heidelberg_(play)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alt Heidelberg (play)">Alt Heidelberg (play)</a></div>
<p>In 1901 <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Meyer-F%C3%B6rster" title="Wilhelm Meyer-Förster">Wilhelm Meyer-Förster</a> wrote the play <i><a href="/wiki/Old_Heidelberg_(play)" title="Old Heidelberg (play)">Old Heidelberg</a></i> which was followed by a large number of film adaptations. It was the basis for <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Romberg" title="Sigmund Romberg">Sigmund Romberg</a>'s 1924 operetta <i><a href="/wiki/The_Student_Prince" title="The Student Prince">The Student Prince</a></i> which was itself turned into a <a href="/wiki/The_Student_Prince_(film)" title="The Student Prince (film)">film of the same title</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="I_Lost_My_Heart_in_Heidelberg">I Lost My Heart in Heidelberg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: I Lost My Heart in Heidelberg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/I_Lost_My_Heart_in_Heidelberg_(song)" title="I Lost My Heart in Heidelberg (song)">I Lost My Heart in Heidelberg (song)</a></div>
<p>The 1925 song "I Lost My Heart in Heidelberg" composed by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Raymond" title="Fred Raymond">Fred Raymond</a> was a major hit and inspired a stage musical and two films. It remains the theme song of Heidelberg.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Heidelberg is one of the centres of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Germany" title="Rugby union in Germany">Rugby union in Germany</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Rugby-Bundesliga_2008-09" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby-Bundesliga 2008-09">2008–09</a>, four out of nine clubs in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby-Bundesliga" title="Rugby-Bundesliga">Rugby-Bundesliga</a> were from Heidelberg, these being <a href="/wiki/RG_Heidelberg" title="RG Heidelberg">RG Heidelberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/SC_Neuenheim" title="SC Neuenheim">SC Neuenheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_RK" title="Heidelberger RK">Heidelberger RK</a> and <a href="/wiki/TSV_Handschuhsheim" title="TSV Handschuhsheim">TSV Handschuhsheim</a>. <a href="/wiki/Heidelberger_TV" title="Heidelberger TV">Heidelberger TV</a> has a rugby department. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Germany" title="Rugby league in Germany">Rugby League Deutschland</a> has two teams based in Heidelberg, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg_Sharks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Heidelberg Sharks (page does not exist)">Heidelberg Sharks</a> formed in 2005 and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rohrbach_Hornets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rohrbach Hornets (page does not exist)">Rohrbach Hornets</a> formed in 2007.</p>
<p>The city is also home to the <a href="/wiki/USC_Heidelberg" title="USC Heidelberg">USC Heidelberg</a>, which won 9 <a href="/wiki/German_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="German Basketball Championship">German Basketball Championships</a> and remains the second most successful team in the history of German professional basketball. Today, the club plays in Germany's second division <a href="/wiki/ProA" title="ProA">ProA</a>. It is primarily known for its youth department which developed several members of <a href="/wiki/Germany%27s_senior_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Germany's senior national basketball team">Germany's senior national basketball team</a>.</p>
<p>Further, Germany's oldest tennis club, which was founded in the year 1890, is located in Heidelberg.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heidelberg is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> (<i>städtepartnerschaft</i>) with:<sup id="cite_ref-TwinsCities_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TwinsCities-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr valign="top">
<td>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/England" title="England"><img alt="England" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/23px-Flag_of_England.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/35px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/46px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="480" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, England, since 1965<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Heidelberg features in the 1968 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Girl_on_a_Motorcycle" title="The Girl on a Motorcycle">The Girl on a Motorcycle</a></i>, the university being the ultimate destination of <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Faithfull" title="Marianne Faithfull">Marianne Faithfull</a>'s character. Heidelberg is the home of a professional <a href="/wiki/Quidditch" title="Quidditch">Quidditch</a> team operating within the fictional <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_universe" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Potter universe">Harry Potter universe</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Harriers" class="mw-redirect" title="Heidelberg Harriers">Heidelberg Harriers</a> have been described as “fiercer than a dragon and twice as clever”.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Heidelberg is the residence of fictional character Nina Fortner/Anna Liebert in the <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a>/<a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Monster_(manga)" title="Monster (manga)">Monster</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Naoki_Urasawa" title="Naoki Urasawa">Naoki Urasawa</a>. Further, its castle forms the setting for the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a>'s story <i><a href="/wiki/The_Awful_German_Language" title="The Awful German Language">The Awful German Language</a></i>. Most of <a href="/wiki/David_Lodge_(author)" title="David Lodge (author)">David Lodge</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Shelter" title="Out of the Shelter">Out of the shelter</a></i> takes place in Heidelberg in 1951 during the American occupation after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The city also features during a mission in the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> strategy game <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Alert_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Alert 3">Red Alert 3</a></i>. Heidelberg also features in <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Maugham" class="mw-redirect" title="Somerset Maugham">Somerset Maugham</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Of_Human_Bondage" title="Of Human Bondage">Of Human Bondage</a></i> and its film versions. Also, "<a href="/wiki/Morris_from_America" title="Morris from America">Morris from America</a>" takes places in Heidelberg.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_inhabitants">Notable inhabitants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Notable inhabitants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_Albrecht_(politician)" title="Ernst Albrecht (politician)">Ernst Albrecht</a> (1930–2014), politician (CDU), Minister-president of Lower Saxony, father of <a href="/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen" title="Ursula von der Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jill_Asemota" title="Jill Asemota">Jill Asemota</a>, German-Nigerian model</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jackson_Browne" title="Jackson Browne">Jackson Browne</a> (born 1948), singer-songwriter and musician born here</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Petar_Beron" title="Petar Beron">Petar Beron</a> (1799–1871), Bulgarian educator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Bunsen" title="Robert Bunsen">Robert Bunsen</a> (1811–1899), German chemist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antje_Duvekot" title="Antje Duvekot">Antje Duvekot</a> (born 1976), singer-songwriter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans-Georg_Gadamer" title="Hans-Georg Gadamer">Hans-Georg Gadamer</a> (1900–2002), German philosopher</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Fassbender" title="Michael Fassbender">Michael Fassbender</a> (born 1977), German-Irish actor born here</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ian_Harding" title="Ian Harding">Ian Harding</a> (born 1986), German actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harald_zur_Hausen" title="Harald zur Hausen">Harald zur Hausen</a> (born 1936), <a href="/wiki/Virology" title="Virology">virologist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Laureate</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dietmar_Hopp" title="Dietmar Hopp">Dietmar Hopp</a> (born 1940), software entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/SAP_SE" title="SAP SE">SAP</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Iqbal" title="Muhammad Iqbal">Muhammad Iqbal</a> (1877–1938), Pakistani poet, philosopher</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Ketterle" title="Wolfgang Ketterle">Wolfgang Ketterle</a> (born 1957), physicist, professor at <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Laureate</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Kirchhof" title="Paul Kirchhof">Paul Kirchhof</a> (born 1943), former Judge in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Constitutional_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Constitutional Court of Germany">Federal Constitutional Court of Germany</a> (<i>Bundesverfassungsgericht</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Kroh" title="Hans Kroh">Hans Kroh</a> (1907–1967), German officer in Wehrmacht and Bundeswehr</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_A._Lamers" title="Karl A. Lamers">Karl A. Lamers</a> (born 1951), politician, former President of the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="NATO Parliamentary Assembly">NATO Parliamentary Assembly</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ananda_Mahidol" title="Ananda Mahidol">Ananda Mahidol</a> (1925–1946), King of Thailand</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Neal" title="Heinrich Neal">Heinrich Neal</a> (1870–1940), German composer, directed the Heidelberg Conservatory of Music</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vasil_Radoslavov" title="Vasil Radoslavov">Vasil Radoslavov</a> (1854–1929), Bulgarian Prime Minister</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">José Rizal</a> (1861–1896), national hero of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christiane_Schmidtmer" title="Christiane Schmidtmer">Christiane Schmidtmer</a> (1939–2003), Hollywood actress and model</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bernd_Schmitt" title="Bernd Schmitt">Bernd Schmitt</a> (born 1957), marketing professor at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Klaus_Sch%C3%BCtz" title="Klaus Schütz">Klaus Schütz</a> (1926–2012), German politician (SPD)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silvia_Renate_Sommerlath" class="mw-redirect" title="Silvia Renate Sommerlath">Silvia Renate Sommerlath</a> (born 1943), <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Sweden">Queen of Sweden</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Speer" title="Albert Speer">Albert Speer</a> (1905–1981), German architect and <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Hitler" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet Hitler">Third Reich minister</a></li>
<li>Ferdinand Thomas (1913–1944), resistance fighter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_J%C3%BCnger" title="Ernst Jünger">Ernst Jünger</a> (1895–1998), German author, officer, botanist and entomologist, famous for his World War I memoir Storm of Steel</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people_who_died_in_Heidelberg">Notable people who died in Heidelberg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Heidelberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notable people who died in Heidelberg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Bunsen" title="Robert Bunsen">Robert Bunsen</a> (1811–1899), German <a href="/wiki/Chemist" title="Chemist">chemist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Ioan_Cuza" title="Alexandru Ioan Cuza">Alexandru Ioan Cuza</a> (3 May 1873), Prince of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, Prince of <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and later <i><a href="/wiki/Domnitor" title="Domnitor">domnitor</a></i> (ruler) of the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Principalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Principalities">Romanian Principalities</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walther_Dahl" title="Walther Dahl">Walther Dahl</a>, (1916–1985), German<a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> ace</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Hierl" title="Konstantin Hierl">Konstantin Hierl</a>, leader of the Reichsarbeitsdienst (24 February 1875 – 23 September 1955)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a> (1885–1945), <a href="/wiki/U.S._Army" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Army">U.S. Army</a> general</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christiane_Schmidtmer" title="Christiane Schmidtmer">Christiane Schmidtmer</a> (1939–2003), German actress</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Felix_Heinrich_Wankel" class="mw-redirect" title="Felix Heinrich Wankel">Felix Heinrich Wankel</a> (1902–1988), <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanical engineer">mechanical engineer</a> and inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Wankel_engine" title="Wankel engine">Wankel engine</a></li>
</ul>
